## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics / nonlinear dynamics (nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, with state variables position x and velocity v, indicating a second-order ODE x'' = dv_dt typical of (non)linear oscillators. Common physics structure is restoring force as a function of x plus damping as a function of v, optionally with time-dependent forcing/parametric modulation in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear (undamped) harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (restoring force proportional to displacement)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (linear viscous damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t + c4) (periodic external forcing)
- Duffing oscillator (hardening/softening spring): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (nonlinear stiffness + viscous damping)
- Bistable (double-well) Duffing form: dv_dt = c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (negative linear stiffness + cubic stabilization)
- Simple pendulum (small/large angle): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(x) - c1 * v (nonlinear trigonometric restoring torque)
- Quadratic (turbulent) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (drag ~ v|v| at higher Reynolds number)
- Coulomb (dry) friction + spring: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * sign(v) (nearly constant-magnitude friction opposing motion)
- Nonlinear spring with piecewise stiffness: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x * Abs(x) - c2 * v (stiffening with |x|)
- Van der Pol oscillator (self-excited): dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v - c2 * x (negative damping at small |x|, positive at large |x|)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent self-excitation): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (amplitude-limiting nonlinear damping)
- Parametrically excited oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness, e.g., Mathieu-type)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring forces often appear as dv_dt depending only on x and being odd in x (e.g., -c*sin(x), -c*x - c*x**3), reflecting symmetry about equilibrium.
- Viscous damping is typically odd in v (e.g., -c*v), guaranteeing energy dissipation for both motion directions.
- High-speed drag commonly uses nonlinear odd damping like -c*v*Abs(v) (stronger dissipation at larger |v|).
- Dry friction is well-modeled by sign(v) or v/(Abs(v)+c) regularizations, producing stick-slip and non-smooth acceleration near v=0.
- Self-excited oscillations correspond to “negative damping” at small amplitude, implemented by factors like (1 - c*x**2)*v or v - c*v**3 to create a stable limit cycle.
- Hardening/softening springs are captured by adding cubic stiffness terms in x, which implies amplitude-dependent frequency (non-isochronous oscillation).
- Periodic external driving typically enters additively as sin(c*t) or cos(c*t), while parametric excitation multiplies x (or v) by a periodic function of t.
- If the system is autonomous (no explicit t), good candidate structures omit t entirely; explicit t terms usually indicate forcing or modulation rather than intrinsic dynamics.
- Bistability and snap-through behavior are suggested by a restoring force with competing linear and cubic terms (e.g., +c*x - c*x**3), yielding multiple equilibria.
- Liénard-type decompositions dv_dt = -f(x)*v - g(x) are common: g(x) sets restoring force, f(x) sets state-dependent damping/excitation.
